In recent years, millimeter-dust rings observed by ALMA have been suggested to have their origin in dust traps, caused by pressure bumps. One of the ways to generate these is by the presence of planets, which lower the gas density along their orbit and create pressure bumps at the edge. We present spatially resolved ALMA Cycle 0 and Cycle 1 observations of CO and CO isotopologues of several famous transitional disks. Gas is found to be present inside the dust cavities, but at a reduced level compared with the gas surface density profile of the outer disk. The dust and gas emission are quantified using the physical-chemical modeling code DALI. In the majority of these disks we find clear evidence for a drop in gas density of at least a factor of 10 inside the cavity, whereas the dust density drops by at least a factor 1000. The CO isotopologue observations reveal that the gas cavities are significantly smaller than the dust cavities. These gas structures suggest clearing by one or more planetary-mass companions.</jats:p>", "DOI": "10.1017/s1743921315006444", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2016, 1, 27]], "date-time": "2016-01-27T11:12:09Z", "timestamp": 1453893129000}, "page": "139-142", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 0, "title": ["Gas Cavities inside Dust Cavities in Disks Inferred from ALMA Observations"], "prefix": "10.1017", "volume": "10", "author": [{"given": "Nienke", "family": "van der Marel", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Ewine F.", "family": "van Dishoeck", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Simon", "family": "Bruderer", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Paola", "family": "Pinilla", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Tim", "family": "van Kempen", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Laura", "family": "Perez", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Andrea", "family": "Isella", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}], "member": "56", "published-online": {"date-parts": [[2016, 1, 27]]}, "reference": [{"key": "S1743921315006444_ref2", "author": "Bruderer", "volume": "559", "first-page": "A46", "year": "2013", "journal-title": "AandA"}, {"key": "S1743921315006444_ref13", "DOI": "10.1093/mnras/180.2.57", "doi-asserted-by": "publisher"}, {"key": "S1743921315006444_ref10", "unstructured": "van der Marel N. , van Dishoeck E. The kinematics, sampled in detail in one case-study, are indicative of non-Keplerian flows, corresponding to warped structures and accretion which may both play a role in the development of cavities. Disk asymmetries seen in the radio continuum are being interpreted in the context of dust segregation via aerodynamic trapping. {"date-parts": [[2019, 9]]}, "abstract": "<jats:p><jats:italic>Context.</jats:italic> The extent of the gas in protoplanetary discs is observed to be universally larger than the extent of the dust. This is often attributed to radial drift and grain growth of the millimetre grains, but line optical depth produces a similar observational signature.</jats:p>\n<jats:p><jats:italic>Aims.</jats:italic> We investigate in which parts of the disc structure parameter space dust evolution and line optical depth are the dominant drivers of the observed gas and dust size difference.</jats:p>\n<jats:p><jats:italic>Methods.</jats:italic> Using the thermochemical model <jats:monospace>DALI</jats:monospace> with dust evolution included we ran a grid of models aimed at reproducing the observed gas and dust size dichotomy.</jats:p>\n<jats:p><jats:italic>Results.</jats:italic> The relation between <jats:italic>R</jats:italic><jats:sub>dust</jats:sub> and dust evolution is non-monotonic and depends on the disc structure. The quantity <jats:italic>R</jats:italic><jats:sub>gas</jats:sub> is directly related to the radius where the CO column density drops below 10<jats:sup>15</jats:sup>\u00a0cm<jats:sup>\u22122</jats:sup> and CO becomes photodissociated; <jats:italic>R</jats:italic><jats:sub>gas</jats:sub> is not affected by dust evolution but scales with the total CO content of the disc. While these cases are rare in current observations, <jats:italic>R</jats:italic><jats:sub>gas</jats:sub>/<jats:italic>R</jats:italic><jats:sub>dust</jats:sub> &gt; 4 is a clear sign of dust evolution and radial drift in discs. For discs with a smaller <jats:italic>R</jats:italic><jats:sub>gas</jats:sub>/<jats:italic>R</jats:italic><jats:sub>dust</jats:sub>, identifying dust evolution from <jats:italic>R</jats:italic><jats:sub>gas</jats:sub>/<jats:italic>R</jats:italic><jats:sub>dust</jats:sub> requires modelling the disc structure including the total CO content. To minimize the uncertainties due to observational factors requires FWHM<jats:sub>beam</jats:sub> &lt; 1\u00d7 the characteristic radius and a peak S/N &gt; 10 on the <jats:sup>12</jats:sup>CO emission moment zero map. For the dust outer radius to enclose most of the disc mass, it should be defined using a high fraction (90\u201395%) of the total flux. For the gas, any radius enclosing &gt;60% of the <jats:sup>12</jats:sup>CO flux contains most of the disc mass.</jats:p>\n<jats:p><jats:italic>Conclusions.</jats:italic> To distinguish radial drift and grain growth from line optical depth effects based on size ratios requires discs to be observed at high enough angular resolution and the disc structure should to be modelled to account for the total CO content of the disc.</jats:p>", "DOI": "10.1051/0004-6361/201834723", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2019, 8, 8]], "date-time": "2019-08-08T18:45:50Z", "timestamp": 1565289950000}, "page": "A79", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 1, "title": ["Gas versus dust sizes of protoplanetary discs: effects of dust evolution"], "prefix": "10.1051", "volume": "629", "author": [{"given": "L.", "family": "Trapman", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "S.", "family": "Facchini", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "M.
